I could have avoided burning the Thanksgiving ham last year, that's for sure.<br><br>Just stick this in your oven, and make sure to check it often and take note of how your oven behaves.<br><br>As an example, here is what I found out about my oven: it takes longer than I thought to preheat (almost 20 minutes), but after 30-40 minutes it is about 25 degrees hotter than I set the dial, and after 45-60 minutes it runs a full 50 degrees hot.<br><br>Which is why I never really noticed before, I rarely bake things for so long.  But you can see how a 5 hour roast would be a huge problem without knowing this.  Likewise you can see how the 5th batch of cookies might burn if you leave it in as long as the 1st batch without adjusting the temperature.<br><br>Now I just adjust the dial accordingly and have no more problems. </div>  </div>        <a class="a-link-normal comment-link" title="0" Hannan</a>   </span> <span class="a-color-secondary"> on November 26, 2012</span></span></div><div id="revData-dpReviewsMostHelpfulAUI-ROL5GPJNWZYTI" class="a-row a-spacing-small"><span class="a-size-mini a-color-state a-text-bold">     Verified Purchase   </span>      <div class="a-section">   This thermometer can only be used hanging.  It can't stay standing for anything, if anything jiggles (like moving the food or the rack) it falls over.  This causes two problems for me:  1 -  Given the age of my oven, there are real variances in the temperature depending on where you are in the oven, so I really need a thermometer that can be set next to the food.  2 - it can only be used when you are using a middle rack... it's too large to fit otherwise. </div>  </div>        <a class="a-link-normal comment-link" title="0"
